<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">BOJ minutes: Several see U.S. risks heightening   </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>146 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>26 December 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>01:06</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"> TOKYO, Dec 26 (Reuters) - Several members of the Bank of
Japan's policy board said downside risks in the U.S. economy were
heightening, according to minutes of the central bank's Nov.
12-13 meeting released on Wednesday.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"> The minutes also showed that one member said inflation
pressures in Japan based on domestic demand were not strong.   </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"> At the previous meeting on Oct. 31, one member said consumer
prices could rise significantly around the start of the fiscal
year from next April due to rises in prices of crude oil and
daily necessities, the minutes showed.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"> The BOJ board kept its key policy rate unchanged at 0.5
percent at both meetings.
 (Reporting by Yuzo Saeki and Leika Kihara)

   </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />JAPAN-ECONOMY/MINUTES|LANGEN|J|ABN|E|RBN|M|D|U|NAT|ABX|BNX|FUN</td></tr>

</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>1124 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>26 December 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>23:00</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"> Following are polls for major Japanese indicators scheduled for
the week of Dec 25-28.
   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"></p><pre class="articlePre"> LOCAL  LOCAL                                     MEDIAN

<p></p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"> Note: Dates and times are local, followed by GMT time. Asterisk*
means GMT is previous day
 HOUSING STARTS
 - Housing starts have plunged since the government adopted
tighter building regulations in June, dragging down third-quarter
economic growth.
 - A poll of 29 economists produced a median forecast of a 28.0
percent decline in housing starts for November from a year
earlier. Forecasts for the fall ranged from 15.8 to 39.8 percent.
 CPI
 - The nationwide core consumer price index rose a modest 0.1
percent in October from a year earlier, the first increase in 10
months, mostly on higher energy and food prices.
 - The Bank of Japan expects consumer price growth to gradually
pick up, although many economists see the central bank delaying
raising rates until well into next year on shaky global markets
and doubts over the strength of Japan's economy.
 - If core CPI, which excludes volatile fresh food prices, rises
0.3 percent in November as forecast, it would be the highest
growth since a 1.8 percent rise in March 1998, when figures were
inflated by a consumption tax hike.
 - Following are forecasts for Tokyo core CPI in December and
nationwide core CPI in November (percent, year-on-year):   </p>

   </pre>
<p></p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph"> HOUSEHOLD SPENDING
 - Overall household spending rose modestly in October from a
year earlier, but a worsening in consumer sentiment has led to
views that personal consumption will lack momentum in the coming
months.
 - Economists warn against reading too much into the data, saying
it is flawed due to bad sampling.
 - A Reuters poll of 30 economists produced a median forecast for
a 0.4 percent increase. Forecasts ranged from a 0.3 percent fall
to a 1.8 percent rise.
 JOBS DATA
 - The unemployment rate has been creeping up from a nine-year
low of 3.6 percent in July, while the number of job offers fell
to a nearly two-year low in October, signalling that improvements
in the job market may be stalling.
 - The jobless rate probably stood at 4.0 percent in November,
unchanged from the previous month, according to a Reuters poll of
31 economists. Their forecasts ranged from 3.9 percent to 4.2
percent.
 - The jobs-to-applicants ratio was probably unchanged from the
previous month at 1.02, meaning there were 102 jobs available per
100 job seekers.
 RETAIL SALES
 - Retail sales rose more than expected in October partly on
strong car sales as some automakers introduced new models.
 - The government changed its assessment on retail sales in
October for the first time since January, saying sales are
recovering. Previously it said they were largely flat.
 - Retail sales probably rose 0.9 percent in November from a year
earlier. The 21 economists polled all predicted rises, ranging
from 0.5 to 1.7 percent.
 INDUSTRIAL PRODUCTION
 - Industrial output has been recovering gradually since falling
in the first quarter of this year, with solid exports to Asia and
Europe offsetting soft shipments to the United States.
 - The poll of 32 economists produced a median forecast for a
month-on-month fall of 1.7 percent. Forecasts ranged from a fall
of 2.8 percent to a rise of 0.2 percent.
 - Following are forecasts for percentage changes in industrial
production in November from October and a year earlier.   </p>

<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">Japan economy can grow 2% in next 4 yrs-govt panel   </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>305 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>26 December 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>11:21</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">TOKYO, Dec 26 (Reuters) - Japan's economy can grow 2 percent or more in the next four years if the government carries out reforms, a draft of a government report on mid-term policy said.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The report said that if the government fails to implement appropriate policy and the global economy slows down, economic growth would only be around 1.0-1.4 percent in the four years from fiscal 2008/09 starting next April to 2011/12.   </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">In nominal terms, the Japanese economy could grow 3 percent or more with a favourable scenario. However, the growth rate might only be around 1.5-1.9 percent or less if things moved in a bad direction, the report said.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The draft was submitted to the government's top advisory panel, the Council on Economic and Fiscal Policy, on Wednesday as a base for policy discussion next year.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"We need to discuss measures to realise economic growth, breaking down the sense of recoil and stagnation," Economics Minister Hiroko Ota quoted Prime Minister Yasuo Fukuda as telling a panel meeting on Wednesday.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The report projected the consumer price index (CPI) will likely rise to around 1.5 percent by 2011/12.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The government last week revised down its economic growth forecast for the current fiscal year to March 30 to 1.3 percent from an earlier estimate of 2.1 percent, blaming the construction slump after stricter building rules were introduced in June. [ID:nT148004]   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The government also forecast the overall CPI to rise 0.3 percent in the next fiscal year, up from 0.2 percent estimated for the current year. (Reporting by Yuzo Saeki, editing by Jacqueline Wong)   </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />JAPAN-ECONOMY/GROWTH|LANGEN|ABN|M|E|RBN|D|J|ABX|RNP|DNP</td></tr>

<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">BOJ Kamezaki: Low rates risky, timely rise needed   </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>148 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>26 December 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>08:17</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">YOKOHAMA, Japan, Dec 26 (Reuters) - Interest rates that are too low have risks and the Bank of Japan needs to raise rates in a timely manner, central bank policy board member Hidetoshi Kamezaki said on Wednesday.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"Interest rates that are too low compared with the real economy carry risks for the future," Kamezaki told a news conference. "The BOJ needs to raise rates in a timely manner.   </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"But at the moment there are uncertainties on the impact of the U.S. slowdown, market turmoil and rising oil prices on the economy," he said.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Kamezaki, a former trading house executive, joined the central bank in April and has been seen as a policy hawk. (Reporting by Hideyuki Sano)   </p>

<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">UPDATE 2-BOJ's Kamezaki: Caution needed amid uncertainty   </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>BY</b> </td><td>By Hideyuki Sano   </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>717 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>26 December 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>07:43</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited   </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">(Adds comments)   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">YOKOHAMA, Japan, Dec 26 (Reuters) - A recently appointed Bank of Japan policy board member said on Wednesday that uncertainty about the global economic outlook is rising, although he added that the central bank's next action would still be to raise interest rates, not cut them.   </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">BOJ board member Hidetoshi Kamezaki, a former private sector executive who has been seen as a policy hawk, said rates need to be raised in a timely manner, sticking to the bank's official line that keeping them at current low levels for too long could have long-term risks.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">But he acknowledged that the Japanese economy's positive cycle of increasing output, income and expenditures was weakening somewhat, underscoring views that the BOJ was in no rush to hike its key policy rate from the current 0.5 percent.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"Interest rates that are too low compared with the real economy carry risks for the future," Kamezaki told a news conference after meeting business leaders in Yokohama, near Tokyo.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"But at the moment there are uncertainties on the impact of the U.S. slowdown, market turmoil and rising oil prices on the economy," he said.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">In his first public speech since he joined the BOJ in April, Kamezaki mostly toed the bank's official line on the economy, saying the Japanese economy is slowing now, partly on the domestic housing slump, but is expected to grow moderately.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Financial markets showed muted response to his comments, with swap contracts on the overnight call rate pricing in less than a 35 percent chance of a rate hike even by the end of next year.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"Kamezaki's remarks were mostly in line with the BOJ board's consensus view, which is that the bank needs to raise rates in the long run but is in no rush to do so," said Masaaki Kanno, chief economist at JPMorgan Securities.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"He is neither extremely dovish nor hawkish, although his remarks on underlying economic conditions seemed somewhat cautious," he said.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">A BOJ rate hike to 0.75 percent, once considered a near certainty by the end of this year, is now seen stalled by growing threats to Japan's economic outlook.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Shaky global financial markets, concern over slowing U.S. growth and rising prices of crude oil and other raw materials are dampening Japan's corporate business sentiment.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The central bank downgraded its economic view last week, the first such major downgrade in three years, saying growth is slowing because of a plunge in house building after tighter construction rules were introduced in June.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Kamezaki said the housing woes could affect production in some construction-related industries.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Falling semiconductor prices may be a sign of oversupply, he said, striking a more cautious tone than the BOJ's official assessment that excess inventory in the high-tech sector has already been worked out.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Kamezaki has voted consistently with the majority not to raise rates since joining the board in April.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">But he has been considered a policy hawk since he said in a newspaper interview in June that the bank should take action promptly once it confirms that growth is set to continue.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Minutes of central bank's Nov. 12-13 meeting released on Wednesday also showed that several members of the bank's nine-member policy board said downside risks in the U.S. economy were heightening, with one member saying it could worsen more than expected on further adjustment in the housing sector.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The BOJ has long said it will raise rates gradually, as its current policy rate of 0.5 percent is so low it could lead to overheating in the economy in the long term.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">The BOJ has said strong growth in the world economy will support Japanese companies' production and exports, which in turn will eventually spill over to households and prompt consumers to spend more.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">But the global credit crunch is seen threatening to knock the U.S. economy into recession and cause a slowdown in growth worldwide, possibly hurting Japanese exports.   </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Domestic consumption has been tame as wages have hardly risen this year despite strong corporate earnings and tight labour markets. (Editing by Mike Miller)   </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />JAPAN-ECONOMY/ (UPDATE 2, PIX)|LANGEN|ABX|BNX|FUN</td></tr>
